\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
abstract base class implementation specifies how to decide volatility structure for additional synthetic rates which are interleaved

implementation specifies how to decide volatility structure for additional synthetic rates which are interleaved

here we work with abcd curves and interpolate the a, b, c and d

Classes for computing derivative of the map taking rates one step to the next with respect to a change in the pseudo-\/root. We do it both numerically and analytically to provide an easy test of the analytic method. This is useful for pathwise vegas.

Evolution is log Euler.

One is tested against the other in Market\+Model\+Test\+::test\+Pathwise\+Vegas

In order to compute market vegas, we need a class that gives the derivative of a swaption implied vol against changes in pseudo-\/root elements. This is that class.

This is tested in the pathwise vegas routine in Market\+Models.\+cpp

When bumping vols, bumping every pseudo-\/root element individually seems excessive so we need to couple some together.

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{MidEquivalent@{MidEquivalent}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!MidEquivalent@{MidEquivalent}}}\Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_ab37ae561efe2ca1a584783cdf6f788aea319bf9f8eaa8afee20ca53e70644dc63}\label{namespace_quant_lib_ab37ae561efe2ca1a584783cdf6f788aea319bf9f8eaa8afee20ca53e70644dc63} 
Mid\+Equivalent&Mid equivalent price, calculated as a) the arithmetic average of bid and ask prices when both are available; b) either the bid or the ask price if any of them is available; c) the last price; or d) the close price. \\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{MidSafe@{MidSafe}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!MidSafe@{MidSafe}}}\Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_ab37ae561efe2ca1a584783cdf6f788aea8cd7df1dd3d25e15365b6ee274a56305}\label{namespace_quant_lib_ab37ae561efe2ca1a584783cdf6f788aea8cd7df1dd3d25e15365b6ee274a56305} 
Mid\+Safe&Safe Mid price, returns the mid price only if both bid and ask are available. \\
\hline

template$<$typename Forward\+Iterator, typename Output\+Iterator$>$ \\
void Quant\+Lib\+::autocorrelations (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Forward\+Iterator}]{begin}{, }\item[{Forward\+Iterator}]{end}{, }\item[{Output\+Iterator}]{out}{, }\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{max\+Lag}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a53c1a019b8cae87b9b3f14e173ac6e02} 
template$<$typename Forward\+Iterator, typename Output\+Iterator$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} Quant\+Lib\+::autocorrelations (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Forward\+Iterator}]{begin}{, }\item[{Forward\+Iterator}]{end}{, }\item[{Output\+Iterator}]{out}{, }\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{max\+Lag}{, }\item[{bool}]{reuse}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Unbiased auto-\/correlations. 

Results are calculated via FFT. The first element of the output is the unbiased sample variance.

This overload accepts non-\/centered data, removes the mean and returns it as a result. The centered sequence is written back into the input sequence if the reuse parameter is true.

\begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
The size of the output sequence must be max\+Lag + 1 
\end{DoxyPrecond}

Exact Bachelier implied volatility

It is calculated using the analytic implied volatility formula of Jaeckel (2017), "{}\+Implied Normal Volatility"{} \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_ada81e127a51181af970327adbbb6a65a}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!bachelierBlackFormulaImpliedVolChoi@{bachelierBlackFormulaImpliedVolChoi}}
\index{bachelierBlackFormulaImpliedVolChoi@{bachelierBlackFormulaImpliedVolChoi}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{bachelierBlackFormulaImpliedVolChoi()}{bachelierBlackFormulaImpliedVolChoi()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_ada81e127a51181af970327adbbb6a65a} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} Quant\+Lib\+::bachelier\+Black\+Formula\+Implied\+Vol\+Choi (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Option\+::\+Type}]{option\+Type}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{strike}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{forward}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{tte}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{bachelier\+Price}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{discount}{ = {\ttfamily 1.0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Approximated Bachelier implied volatility

It is calculated using the analytic implied volatility approximation of J. Choi, K Kim and M. Kwak (2009), “\+Numerical Approximation of the Implied \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_ae3abfa256de5aa2b506ab6bda014e4dc}{Volatility} Under Arithmetic Brownian Motion”, Applied Math. Finance, 16(3), pp. 261-\/268. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a87ef92d0a51e8d41af30fe18059b5c00}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!bachelierBlackFormulaStdDevDerivative@{bachelierBlackFormulaStdDevDerivative}}
\index{bachelierBlackFormulaStdDevDerivative@{bachelierBlackFormulaStdDevDerivative}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{bachelierBlackFormulaStdDevDerivative()}{bachelierBlackFormulaStdDevDerivative()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a87ef92d0a51e8d41af30fe18059b5c00} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} Quant\+Lib\+::bachelier\+Black\+Formula\+Std\+Dev\+Derivative (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{strike}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{forward}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{std\+Dev}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{discount}{ = {\ttfamily 1.0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Bachelier formula for standard deviation derivative \begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
instead of volatility it uses standard deviation, i.\+e. volatility\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}sqrt(time\+To\+Maturity), and it returns the derivative with respect to the standard deviation. If T is the time to maturity Black vega would be black\+Std\+Dev\+Derivative(strike, forward, std\+Dev)\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}sqrt(T) 
\end{DoxyWarning}

Stefanica \href{https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=2922742}{\texttt{ https\+://papers.\+ssrn.\+com/sol3/papers.\+cfm?abstract\+\_\+id=2922742}} \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a324317d9e89ca72d487ae115e7cdaf53}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!blackFormulaImpliedStdDevChambers@{blackFormulaImpliedStdDevChambers}}

\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} Quant\+Lib\+::black\+Formula\+Implied\+Std\+Dev\+Chambers (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const ext\+::shared\+\_\+ptr$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_plain_vanilla_payoff}{Plain\+Vanilla\+Payoff}} $>$ \&}]{payoff}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{forward}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{black\+Price}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{black\+Atm\+Price}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{discount}{ = {\ttfamily 1.0}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{displacement}{ = {\ttfamily 0.0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

It is calculated following "{}\+An improved approach to computing implied volatility"{}, Chambers, Nawalkha, The Financial Review, 2001, 89-\/100. Black 1976 implied standard deviation, i.\+e. volatility\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}sqrt(time\+To\+Maturity)

"{}\+An Adaptive Successive Over-\/relaxation Method for Computing the \+Black-\/\+Scholes Implied Volatility"{} M. Li, \href{http://mpra.ub.uni-muenchen.de/6867/}{\texttt{ http\+://mpra.\+ub.\+uni-\/muenchen.\+de/6867/}}

Starting point of the iteration is calculated based on

"{}\+An Explicit Implicit Volatility Formula"{} R. Radoicic, D. Stefanica, \href{https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=2908494}{\texttt{ https\+://papers.\+ssrn.\+com/sol3/papers.\+cfm?abstract\+\_\+id=2908494}} \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_adf6bca73cd43adabf366efa466f5fa85}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!blackFormulaStdDevDerivative@{blackFormulaStdDevDerivative}}

Black 1976 formula for standard deviation derivative \begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
instead of volatility it uses standard deviation, i.\+e. volatility\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}sqrt(time\+To\+Maturity), and it returns the derivative with respect to the standard deviation. If T is the time to maturity Black vega would be black\+Std\+Dev\+Derivative(strike, forward, std\+Dev)\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}sqrt(T) 
\end{DoxyWarning}

(bucket) PV01 sensitivity analysis for a (single) \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_simple_quote}{Simple\+Quote} 

returns a pair of first and second derivative values calculated as prescribed by \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis}. Second derivative might not be available depending on \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis} value.

Empty quantities vector is considered as unit vector. The same if the vector is of size one.

bucket PV01 sensitivity analysis for a \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_simple_quote}{Simple\+Quote} vector 

returns a pair of first and second derivative vectors calculated as prescribed by \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis}. Second derivative might not be available depending on \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis} value.

Empty quantities vector is considered as unit vector. The same if the vector is of size one.

The (bucket) Simple\+Quotes are tweaked one by one separately.

void Quant\+Lib\+::bucket\+Analysis (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} $>$ \&}]{delta\+Vector}{, }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} $>$ \&}]{gamma\+Vector}{, }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} $>$ \&}]{reference\+Values}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_handle}{Handle}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_simple_quote}{Simple\+Quote}} $>$ \&}]{quote}{, }\item[{const std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_handle}{Handle}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_quote}{Quote}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{parameters}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{shift}{ = {\ttfamily 0.0001}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis}}}]{type}{ = {\ttfamily Centered}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



(bucket) parameters\textquotesingle{} sensitivity analysis for a (single) \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_simple_quote}{Simple\+Quote} 

returns a vector (one element for each paramet) of pair of first and second derivative values calculated as prescribed by \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis}. Second derivative might not be available depending on \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis} value.

Empty quantities vector is considered as unit vector. The same if the vector is of size one.

void Quant\+Lib\+::bucket\+Analysis (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::vector$<$ std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{delta\+Matrix}{, }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{gamma\+Matrix}{, }\item[{const std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_handle}{Handle}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_simple_quote}{Simple\+Quote}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{quotes}{, }\item[{const std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_handle}{Handle}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_quote}{Quote}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{parameters}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{shift}{ = {\ttfamily 0.0001}, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis}}}]{type}{ = {\ttfamily Centered}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



bucket parameters\textquotesingle{} sensitivity analysis for a \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_simple_quote}{Simple\+Quote} vector 

returns a vector (one element for each paramet) of pair of first and second derivative vectors calculated as prescribed by \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis}. Second derivative might not be available depending on \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis} value.

Empty quantities vector is considered as unit vector. The same if the vector is of size one.

The (bucket) Simple\+Quotes are tweaked one by one separately.

\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000037}{Deprecated}}]Out of scope; copy this function in your codebase if needed. Deprecated in version 1.\+36. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
\Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_ac7d105585f943dd8bfca27d63ce2bdff}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!cdsMaturity@{cdsMaturity}}
\index{cdsMaturity@{cdsMaturity}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{cdsMaturity()}{cdsMaturity()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_ac7d105585f943dd8bfca27d63ce2bdff} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_date}{Date}} Quant\+Lib\+::cds\+Maturity (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_date}{Date}} \&}]{trade\+Date}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_period}{Period}} \&}]{tenor}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_quant_lib_1_1_date_generation_a3fee9b3c834b0d3be240d05886ac2f6e}{Date\+Generation\+::\+Rule}}}]{rule}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Return the CDS maturity date given the CDS trade date, {\ttfamily trade\+Date}, the CDS {\ttfamily tenor} and a CDS {\ttfamily rule}.

A null date is returned when a {\ttfamily rule} of {\ttfamily CDS2015} and a {\ttfamily tenor} length of zero fail to yield a valid CDS maturity date.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
An exception will be thrown if the {\ttfamily rule} is not {\ttfamily CDS2015}, {\ttfamily CDS} or {\ttfamily Old\+CDS}.

An exception will be thrown if the {\ttfamily rule} is {\ttfamily Old\+CDS} and a {\ttfamily tenor} of 0 months is provided. This restriction can be removed if 0M tenor was available before the CDS Big Bang 2009.

An exception will be thrown if the {\ttfamily tenor} is not a multiple of 3 months. For the avoidance of doubt, a {\ttfamily tenor} of 0 months is supported. 
\end{DoxyWarning}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a8c358786ff7da50c785ca5a003b1c9c1} 
bool Quant\+Lib\+::close (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{x}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{y}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Follows somewhat the advice of Knuth on checking for floating-\/point equality. The closeness relationship is\+:    \[\mathrm{close}(x,y,n) \equiv |x-y| \leq \varepsilon |x|
                      \wedge |x-y| \leq \varepsilon |y|
\] where $ \varepsilon $ is $ n $ times the machine accuracy; $ n $ equals 42 if not given. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_acba7cc9670305b8b6164bc87319313de}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!close\_enough@{close\_enough}}
\index{close\_enough@{close\_enough}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}

                        \vee |x-y| \leq \varepsilon |y|

Exponential correlation L = long term correlation beta = exponential decay of correlation between far away forward rates gamma = exponent for time to go t = time dependence \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_aff8e33130b0e7222fca99ceeffe94235}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!factorReduction@{factorReduction}}
\index{factorReduction@{factorReduction}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{factorReduction()}{factorReduction()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_aff8e33130b0e7222fca99ceeffe94235} 
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}} $>$ Quant\+Lib\+::factor\+Reduction (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}}}]{mtrx}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_af4cc4ef40b52c17cc455ead2a97aedb3}{Size}}}]{max\+Iters}{ = {\ttfamily 25}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Iterative procedure to compute a correlation matrix reduction to a single factor dependence vector by minimizing the residuals.

It assumes that such a reduction is possible, notice that if the dependence can not be reduced to one factor the correlation factors might be above 1.

The matrix passed is destroyed.

See for instance\+: "{}\+Modern Factor Analysis"{}, Harry H. Harman, University Of Chicago Press, 1976. Chapter 9 is relevant to this context. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a505d64f84a4000847f8f04ee60398665}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!getCovariance@{getCovariance}}
\index{getCovariance@{getCovariance}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getCovariance()}{getCovariance()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a505d64f84a4000847f8f04ee60398665} 
template$<$class Data\+Iterator$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} Quant\+Lib\+::get\+Covariance (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Data\+Iterator}]{std\+Dev\+Begin}{, }\item[{Data\+Iterator}]{std\+Dev\+End}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \&}]{corr}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{tolerance}{ = {\ttfamily 1.0e-\/12}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Calculation of covariance from correlation and standard deviations. 

Combines the correlation matrix and the vector of standard deviations to return the covariance matrix.

Note that only the symmetric part of the correlation matrix is used. Also it is assumed that the diagonal member of the correlation matrix equals one.

\begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
The correlation matrix must be symmetric with the diagonal members equal to one.
\end{DoxyPrecond}

Reference\+: \href{http://de.mathworks.com/help/matlab/ref/pinv.html}{\texttt{ http\+://de.\+mathworks.\+com/help/matlab/ref/pinv.\+html}} \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moore\%E2\%80\%93Penrose_pseudoinverse}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Moore\%\+E2\%80\%93\+Penrose\+\_\+pseudoinverse}} \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a651914a43b45e390e00a4dfa3b990b8b}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!operator==@{operator==}}
\index{operator==@{operator==}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator==()}{operator==()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a651914a43b45e390e00a4dfa3b990b8b} 
bool Quant\+Lib\+::operator== (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_default_event}{Default\+Event}} \&}]{lhs}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_default_event}{Default\+Event}} \&}]{rhs}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Two credit events are the same independently of their settlement member data. This has the side effect of overwritting different settlements from the same credit event when, say, inserting in a map. But on the other hand one given event can only have one settlement. This means we can not have two restructuring events on a bond on the same date. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a0c621e4b0c7c55dd9d5d79171cc3764c}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!operator==@{operator==}}
\index{operator==@{operator==}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator==()}{operator==()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a0c621e4b0c7c55dd9d5d79171cc3764c} 
bool Quant\+Lib\+::operator== (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_default_type}{Default\+Type}} \&}]{lhs}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_default_type}{Default\+Type}} \&}]{rhs}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Equality is the criteria for indexing the curves. This depends only on the atomic types and not on idiosincracies of derived type as mentioned in the functional documentation (specific event characteristics are relevant to credit event matching but not to the probability meaning). operator== is also used to remove duplicates in some containers. This ensures we do not have two equal events (despite having different characteristics) in those containers. This makes sense, theres no logic in having two \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_failure_to_pay}{Failure\+To\+Pay} in a contract even if they have different characteristics. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_abd5a6a180249e9d37d62387fbdcbe288}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!parallelAnalysis@{parallelAnalysis}}

parallel shift PV01 sensitivity analysis for a \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_simple_quote}{Simple\+Quote} vector

Second derivative might not be available depending on \doxylink{namespace_quant_lib_aec640f352a6039438786a95fc53edb98}{Sensitivity\+Analysis} value.

Empty quantities vector is considered as unit vector. The same if the vector is just one single element equal to one.

All Simple\+Quotes are tweaked together in a parallel fashion.

\Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_ada34a1f564ec5842f47a4f1d171fc0fb}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!previousTwentieth@{previousTwentieth}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_ada34a1f564ec5842f47a4f1d171fc0fb}

Helper function for returning the date on or before date {\ttfamily d} that is the 20th of the month and obeserves the given date generation {\ttfamily rule} if it is relevant. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_ac3c71fcacccbdc38dcf3e5d286bd75d5}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!qrDecomposition@{qrDecomposition}}
\index{qrDecomposition@{qrDecomposition}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{qrDecomposition()}{qrDecomposition()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_ac3c71fcacccbdc38dcf3e5d286bd75d5} 
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_af4cc4ef40b52c17cc455ead2a97aedb3}{Size}} $>$ Quant\+Lib\+::qr\+Decomposition (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \&}]{A}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \&}]{q}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \&}]{r}{, }\item[{bool}]{pivot}{ = {\ttfamily true}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



QR decompoisition. 

This implementation is based on MINPACK (\href{http://www.netlib.org/minpack}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+netlib.\+org/minpack}}, \href{http://www.netlib.org/cephes/linalg.tgz}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+netlib.\+org/cephes/linalg.\+tgz}})

This subroutine uses householder transformations with column pivoting (optional) to compute a qr factorization of the m by n matrix A. That is, qrfac determines an orthogonal matrix q, a permutation matrix p, and an upper trapezoidal matrix r with diagonal elements of nonincreasing magnitude, such that A\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}p = q\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}r.

Return value ipvt is an integer array of length n, which defines the permutation matrix p such that A\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}p = q\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}r. Column j of p is column ipvt(j) of the identity matrix.

See lmdiff.\+cpp for further details. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a91d2a9f5f45584ed32c5804d1a8c18a0}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!qrSolve@{qrSolve}}
\index{qrSolve@{qrSolve}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{qrSolve()}{qrSolve()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a91d2a9f5f45584ed32c5804d1a8c18a0} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_array}{Array}} Quant\+Lib\+::qr\+Solve (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} \&}]{a}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_array}{Array}} \&}]{b}{, }\item[{bool}]{pivot}{ = {\ttfamily true}, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_array}{Array}} \&}]{d}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_array}{Array}}()}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



QR Solve. 

This implementation is based on MINPACK (\href{http://www.netlib.org/minpack}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+netlib.\+org/minpack}}, \href{http://www.netlib.org/cephes/linalg.tgz}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+netlib.\+org/cephes/linalg.\+tgz}})

Given an m by n matrix A, an n by n diagonal matrix d, and an m-\/vector b, the problem is to determine an x which solves the system

A\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}x = b , d\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}x = 0 ,

in the least squares sense.

d is an input array of length n which must contain the diagonal elements of the matrix d.

See lmdiff.\+cpp for further details. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a3b178f11dc8c453a496d4d808f7dad71}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!setCouponPricers@{setCouponPricers}}
\index{setCouponPricers@{setCouponPricers}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setCouponPricers()}{setCouponPricers()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a3b178f11dc8c453a496d4d808f7dad71} 
void Quant\+Lib\+::set\+Coupon\+Pricers (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a14f786c47ee979097c448d96b2defaab}{Leg}} \&}]{leg}{, }\item[{const ext\+::shared\+\_\+ptr$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_floating_rate_coupon_pricer}{Floating\+Rate\+Coupon\+Pricer}} $>$ \&}]{}{, }\item[{const ext\+::shared\+\_\+ptr$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_floating_rate_coupon_pricer}{Floating\+Rate\+Coupon\+Pricer}} $>$ \&}]{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

set the first matching pricer (if any) to each coupon of the leg \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a2133512f1d127edb6a8231a1c055465e}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!simplifyNotificationGraph@{simplifyNotificationGraph}}
\index{simplifyNotificationGraph@{simplifyNotificationGraph}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{simplifyNotificationGraph()}{simplifyNotificationGraph()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a2133512f1d127edb6a8231a1c055465e} 
void Quant\+Lib\+::simplify\+Notification\+Graph (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_instrument}{Instrument}} \&}]{instrument}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a14f786c47ee979097c448d96b2defaab}{Leg}} \&}]{leg}{, }\item[{bool}]{unregister\+Coupons}{ = {\ttfamily false}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Utility function to optimize the observability graph of an instrument. 

This function unregisters the given instrument from the given cashflows and instead registers with the observables of the cashflows. This is safe to do if


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item the coupon pricers of the cashflows are set before the function is called and never updated afterwards
\item the cashflows are not themselves originating notifications, i.\+e. they only pass through notifications from their observables (which is usually the case)
\item the set of cashflows does not dynamically change (usually satisfied as well)
\end{DoxyItemize}

If unregister\+Coupons is set to true, all given cashflows are in addition unregistered from all their observables. This can be done


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item if the coupons are not asked for results directly
\item if deep\+Update() is called on the instrument before retrieving a result; to determine whether the result might have changed, is\+Calculated() can be called on the instrument.
\end{DoxyItemize}

There are overloads of this function for specific instrument types like \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_swap}{Swap}, \doxylink{class_quant_lib_1_1_bond}{Bond}. \Hypertarget{namespace_quant_lib_a573628be8b94717868e2c6a1058cd4d3}\index{QuantLib@{QuantLib}!triangularAnglesParametrization@{triangularAnglesParametrization}}
\index{triangularAnglesParametrization@{triangularAnglesParametrization}!QuantLib@{QuantLib}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{triangularAnglesParametrization()}{triangularAnglesParametrization()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_a573628be8b94717868e2c6a1058cd4d3} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} Quant\+Lib\+::triangular\+Angles\+Parametrization (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_array}{Array}} \&}]{angles}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_af4cc4ef40b52c17cc455ead2a97aedb3}{Size}}}]{matrix\+Size}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_af4cc4ef40b52c17cc455ead2a97aedb3}{Size}}}]{rank}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the Triangular Angles Parametrized correlation matrix. 

The matrix $ m $ is filled with values corresponding to angles given in the $ angles $ vector. See equation (24) in "{}\+Parameterizing correlations\+: a geometric interpretation"{} by Francesco Rapisarda, Damiano Brigo, Fabio Mercurio

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item the correctness of the results is tested by reproducing known good data.
\item the correctness of the results is tested by checking returned values against numerical calculations. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\end{DoxyRefDesc}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{namespace_quant_lib_af62ddda3dd7e71796de3b731df769228} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_quant_lib_1_1_matrix}{Matrix}} Quant\+Lib\+::triangular\+Angles\+Parametrization\+Rank\+Three (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{alpha}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{t0}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_a372ac5c1a422a6b276fe0552d4d83f50}{Real}}}]{epsilon}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_quant_lib_af4cc4ef40b52c17cc455ead2a97aedb3}{Size}}}]{nb\+Rows}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Returns the rank reduced Triangular Angles Parametrized correlation matrix. 

The matrix $ m $ is filled with values corresponding to angles corresponding to the 3D spherical spiral parameterized by $ alpha $, $ t0 $, $ epsilon $ values. See equation (32) in "{}\+Parameterizing correlations\+: a geometric interpretation"{} by Francesco Rapisarda, Damiano Brigo, Fabio Mercurio

\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Test}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{test__test000055}{Test}}]
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item the correctness of the results is tested by reproducing known good data.
\item the correctness of the results is tested by checking returned values against numerical calculations. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\end{DoxyRefDesc}
